\u003cem\u003epast\u003c/em\u003e. In production, only past data exists. Shuffled CV consistently overestimates performance — Stage 15 showed contrastive learning achieved MAE 4.81 with \"unified\" (shuffled) evaluation but 14.85+ with honest LOSO. This 3x gap is pure data leakage.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImplementation (\u003ccode\u003etemporal_cv.py\u003c/code\u003e):\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003echronological_split()\u003c/code\u003e: Sort by timestamp, train on first 70%, test on last 30%\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eexpanding_window_validation()\u003c/code\u003e: Train on samples 1..K, predict K+1, then 1..K+1 predict K+2, etc.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThreshold: expanding-window if n\u0026gt;=50 (enough windows), otherwise 70/30\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy LOSO Is the Honest Population Benchmark\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-loso-is-the-honest-population-benchmark\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why LOSO Is the Honest Population Benchmark\" href=\"#why-loso-is-the-honest-population-benchmark\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLeave-One-Subject-Out cross-validation tests generalization to \u003cem\u003eunseen individuals\u003c/em\u003e. This is the only valid test for a population model because production users are never in the training set. All 22 stages report LOSO as the primary metric. Result: best population LOSO is SVR MAE 12.48, r=-0.098 — effectively no signal.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy Held-Out Validation (80/20 Chronological Blind)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-held-out-validation-8020-chronological-blind\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why Held-Out Validation (80/20 Chronological Blind)\" href=\"#why-held-out-validation-8020-chronological-blind\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAdded in Stage 22 (\u003ccode\u003etools/validate_held_out.py\u003c/code\u003e) as the strictest personal model test. Train on first 80% of a user's data, predict last 20% — data the model has never seen, in chronological order. Result: a0456651 GP MAE 7.92, r=0.604, p=0.001 — first model to pass the signal gate on properly held-out data.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e2. Signal Detection Gate\" href=\"#2-signal-detection-gate\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eThree-Part AND Logic: r\u0026gt;0.3 AND improvement\u0026gt;10% AND p\u0026lt;0.05\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-three-part-and-logic-r03-and-improvement10-and-p005\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Three-Part AND Logic: r\u0026gt;0.3 AND improvement\u0026gt;10% AND p\u0026lt;0.05\" href=\"#three-part-and-logic-r03-and-improvement10-and-p005\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAll three must pass simultaneously. This prevents false discovery across 22 stages of testing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003er \u0026gt; 0.3 (correlation threshold):\u003c/strong\u003e\nDetects meaningful linear association without requiring strong signal. Below 0.3, the correlation explains \u0026lt;9% of variance — indistinguishable from noise on small samples. This is conservative: clinical biomarkers typically require r\u0026gt;0.5, but we're searching for signal, not certifying a device.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eimprovement \u0026gt; 10% (over mean baseline):\u003c/strong\u003e\nFormula: \u003ccode\u003e(baseline_mae - model_mae) / baseline_mae\u003c/code\u003e. The mean baseline (predict user's mean glucose for everything) is surprisingly hard to beat. A model that only improves 5% isn't worth the complexity — the improvement must be clinically meaningful, not just statistically detectable.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ep \u0026lt; 0.05 (permutation test, 1000 shuffles):\u003c/strong\u003e\nDistribution-free significance test. Shuffle glucose labels 1000 times, refit model each time, count how often shuffled r \u0026gt;= observed r. No Gaussian assumption. This catches cases where a high r is an artifact of small sample size or temporal autocorrelation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResult:\u003c/strong\u003e 0/22 population stages pass. GP personal models pass for 1/2 live users (a0456651 with 250+ samples).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e3. Gaussian Process: Physics-Informed Kernel\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-3-gaussian-process-physics-informed-kernel\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 3. After 22 stages showing linear models can't capture the signal, Stage 19 tested GP with nonlinear kernels. Result: GP beats Ridge for 7/10 subjects. The key insight: the voice-glucose relationship is nonlinear and subject-specific — exactly what GP kernels capture.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKernel Architecture (\u003ccode\u003ephysics_gp.py\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-kernel-architecture-physics_gppy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Kernel Architecture (physics_gp.py)\" href=\"#kernel-architecture-physics_gppy\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"K = C(1.0) * RBF(length_scale=[per-feature]) + WhiteKernel(noise=0.5)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eK = C(1.0) * RBF(length_scale=[per-feature]) + WhiteKernel(noise=0.5)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePhysics-informed length scales:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePITCH features (pitch_mean, pitch_std, f0_cv, jitter_local): length_scale=1.5 (shorter = more sensitive). Motivated by Kaufman 2024 finding that F0 increases 0.02 Hz per mg/dL.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVOICE features (mfcc_0, mfcc_1, spectral_centroid, shimmer_approx, hnr, voiced_ratio): length_scale=2.5 (longer = less certain about relevance). These features have weaker theoretical links to glucose.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eBlending Schedule\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-blending-schedule\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Blending Schedule\" href=\"#blending-schedule\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003en\u0026lt;10: Ridge only (GP needs minimum data for stable kernel estimation)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003en=10-20: Linear blend from 5% GP to 100% GP\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003en\u0026gt;20: GP fully takes over\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhy n=10 minimum:\u003c/strong\u003e GP has O(n^3) complexity and requires sufficient data to estimate kernel hyperparameters. Below 10 samples, the kernel optimization is underdetermined and produces unreliable uncertainty estimates.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eProduction Evidence\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-production-evidence\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Production Evidence\" href=\"#production-evidence\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea0456651 (243 cal): GP MAE 7.15, r=0.779 — passes signal gate\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSame user, Ridge: MAE 13.05, r=0.09 — fails signal gate\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe signal is GP-specific: the nonlinear kernel captures patterns Ridge cannot.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e4. 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eenergy_mean (index 86) is hardware-dependent — it scales with microphone gain, volume settings, and device distance. A user switching from iPhone to laptop would shift energy_mean dramatically, contaminating the personal model. shimmer_approx (index 99) measures the same amplitude domain but is normalized (ratio of consecutive periods), making it gain-independent.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy Not All 103 Features?\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-not-all-103-features\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why Not All 103 Features?\" href=\"#why-not-all-103-features\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e843 samples / 103 features = 8.2:1 ratio. This is borderline safe for regularized models but fragile. Stages 13-21b tested 2,500+ feature combinations (HuBERT 2304-dim, nonlinear 68-dim, contrastive embeddings, SEED 141-dim). All produced 0 signal improvement on the population level. The bottleneck is data density per user, not feature expressiveness.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy edge_10 Is Legacy\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-edge_10-is-legacy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why edge_10 Is Legacy\" href=\"#why-edge_10-is-legacy\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe original edge_10 set was chosen for on-device computation speed, not signal quality. It included energy_mean (hardware-dependent), formant_f1_mean (unreliable from short clips), and f0_slope (noisy estimate). personal_10 was selected in Stage 22 by analyzing which canonical features best align with GP kernel physics priors and are gain-independent.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e5. Data Pipeline Decisions\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-5-data-pipeline-decisions\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 5. Data Pipeline Decisions\" href=\"#5-data-pipeline-decisions\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" matching window. At 60 minutes, glucose can change 60-180 mg/dL — pairing a voice sample with a glucose reading from an hour later is scientifically invalid.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLiterature standard: Lehmann 2026 (Diabetes Care) and Kaufman 2024 (Sci Rep) use ≤15 minutes. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH recommends \"within 5 min\" for future collection.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e±15 minutes is a practical compromise: strict enough to be scientifically valid, loose enough to retain adequate samples from historical data with imprecise timestamps. Result: 843 matched samples from \u003ccode\u003erematch_strict_v2.py\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy No Voice Activity Detection (VAD)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-no-voice-activity-detection-vad\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why No Voice Activity Detection (VAD)\" href=\"#why-no-voice-activity-detection-vad\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTested empirically:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWithout VAD: MAE 10.24, r=0.368\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWith VAD: MAE 10.47, r=0.343\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eVAD \u003cem\u003ehurts\u003c/em\u003e. Pauses contain glucose-related information — speech hesitancy, cognitive processing speed, and autonomic effects on breathing patterns are all potential signals that VAD discards. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH explicitly notes: \"Pauses contain glucose-related information.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy No Data Augmentation\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-no-data-augmentation\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why No Data Augmentation\" href=\"#why-no-data-augmentation\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe v5 pipeline tested time-stretching and pitch-shifting augmentation. Performance degraded. Rationale: the glucose signal (if it exists) resides in natural vocal characteristics — F0 perturbation, jitter, shimmer, spectral shape. Artificially distorting these destroys exactly the features we're trying to learn from.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e6. balances model complexity with sample size. Small personal datasets (n\u0026lt;30) are particularly prone to overfitting with 10 features. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH notes this is \"an arbitrary heuristic, never formally validated\" — it was tuned from original 10/n to 100/n based on empirical testing with live users.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e7. 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eClinical hypoglycemia is defined as \u0026lt;70 mg/dL, but our dataset has only 7 samples below 70 versus 45 below 80. Training a classifier on 7 positive samples is unreliable. The 80 mg/dL threshold is a pragmatic choice to have sufficient training data while still detecting clinically relevant low glucose events. Future: lower to \u0026lt;70 once 20+ sub-70 samples are available per user.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eThree-Layer Architecture\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-three-layer-architecture\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Three-Layer Architecture\" href=\"#three-layer-architecture\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRuleBasedHypoDetector\u003c/strong\u003e: 5 biomarker rules (high pitch variability, high jitter, low F0, low energy, low voiced ratio). Alert when \u0026gt;=2 fire. No training needed — works from calibration 1.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eClassifierHypoDetector\u003c/strong\u003e: LogisticRegression + SMOTE (handles class imbalance). Gated by AUROC \u0026gt; 0.65 with \u0026gt;=80% sensitivity threshold. Only activates when gate passes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHybridHypoDetector\u003c/strong\u003e: If classifier is active and passes gate, use classifier OR rules. If classifier fails gate, fall back to rules only.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy SMOTE\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-smote\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why SMOTE\" href=\"#why-smote\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHypo events are rare (45/843 = 5.3%). Without oversampling, LogReg ignores the minority class. SMOTE synthesizes artificial hypo samples in feature space. The AUROC \u0026gt; 0.65 gate ensures we don't deploy a classifier that's just guessing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResults:\u003c/strong\u003e Population AUROC 0.516 (fails gate). Personal: 4/6 subjects pass (Margarita 0.781, Sybille 0.938, Wolf 0.794, Darav 0.760).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e8. JS, verify EVERY parameter (log base, mel formula, normalization flags) against the reference implementation. Comments saying \"matches librosa\" don't guarantee it. 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e95% prediction intervals are too wide for clinical utility — \"your glucose is between 60 and 180\" is useless. 80% intervals are tighter and more actionable. The trade-off: 20% of true values fall outside the interval, but the interval itself is narrow enough to guide decisions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImplementation:\u003c/strong\u003e Quantile regression learns upper/lower bounds from data. No Gaussian assumption (voice features and glucose are both skewed). Stage 19 results: 80.9% average coverage (target 90%), average width 52.9 mg/dL.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e11. dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eStages 1-12: Pipeline setup, Edge Impulse debunked (data leakage), infrastructure\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eStage 13: HuBERT, Glottal, MAML — 0/9 A personal model trained on iPhone Safari data will perform poorly on Chrome Desktop data — the feature distributions shift.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSolution (\u003ccode\u003e_filter_device_change()\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-solution-_filter_device_change\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Solution (_filter_device_change())\" href=\"#solution-_filter_device_change\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGroup calibrations by device fingerprint: \u003ccode\u003e{os}_{browser}_{platform}\u003c/code\u003e. When the newest device has 15+ samples, drop all samples from older devices. This prevents cross-device feature contamination while ensuring the model always has enough data from the current device.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy 15 Samples\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-15-samples\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why 15 Samples\" href=\"#why-15-samples\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBelow 15, dropping old data might leave too few samples for reliable Ridge/GP fitting. Above 15, the new device has enough data to stand alone. This threshold was chosen to balance device purity against sample scarcity.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e13. dir=\"auto\"\u003eSoft Gate (Not Hard Gate)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-soft-gate-not-hard-gate\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Soft Gate (Not Hard Gate)\" href=\"#soft-gate-not-hard-gate\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe SDK's \u003ccode\u003eaddCalibration()\u003c/code\u003e checks four quality criteria:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eDuration \u0026lt; 2s (too short for reliable features)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVoiced ratio \u0026lt; 0.25 (mostly silence/noise)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eEnergy \u0026gt; 0.5 (clipping)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eEnergy \u0026lt; 0.001 (near-silence)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFailures produce warnings but \u003cstrong\u003estill store the calibration\u003c/strong\u003e. Rationale: rejecting data loses information that might be valuable. Instead, quality scores are passed as sample weights to the GP model — low-quality samples have higher noise variance, reducing their influence without discarding them entirely.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e14. ONVOX Technical Rationale","*Written: Mar 22, 2026 — Covers all decisions through Stage 22*","","This document explains WHY every major technical decision was made, grounded in empirical evidence, research literature, and lessons from 22 research stages on 843 samples across 11 subjects.","","---","","## 1. Validation Methodology","","### Why Chronological Splits (Not Shuffled CV)","","Standard k-fold CV and LOO-CV train on *future* data to predict the *past*. In production, only past data exists. Shuffled CV consistently overestimates performance — Stage 15 showed contrastive learning achieved MAE 4.81 with \"unified\" (shuffled) evaluation but 14.85+ with honest LOSO. This 3x gap is pure data leakage.","","**Implementation (`temporal_cv.py`):**","- `chronological_split()`: Sort by timestamp, train on first 70%, test on last 30%","- `expanding_window_validation()`: Train on samples 1..K, predict K+1, then 1..K+1 predict K+2, etc.","- Threshold: expanding-window if n\u003e=50 (enough windows), otherwise 70/30","","### Why LOSO Is the Honest Population Benchmark","","Leave-One-Subject-Out cross-validation tests generalization to *unseen individuals*. This is the only valid test for a population model because production users are never in the training set. All 22 stages report LOSO as the primary metric. Result: best population LOSO is SVR MAE 12.48, r=-0.098 — effectively no signal.","","### Why Held-Out Validation (80/20 Chronological Blind)","","Added in Stage 22 (`tools/validate_held_out.py`) as the strictest personal model test. Train on first 80% of a user's data, predict last 20% — data the model has never seen, in chronological order. Result: a0456651 GP MAE 7.92, r=0.604, p=0.001 — first model to pass the signal gate on properly held-out data.","","---","","## 2. Signal Detection Gate","","### Three-Part AND Logic: r\u003e0.3 AND improvement\u003e10% AND p\u003c0.05","","All three must pass simultaneously. This prevents false discovery across 22 stages of testing.","","**r \u003e 0.3 (correlation threshold):**","Detects meaningful linear association without requiring strong signal. Below 0.3, the correlation explains \u003c9% of variance — indistinguishable from noise on small samples. This is conservative: clinical biomarkers typically require r\u003e0.5, but we're searching for signal, not certifying a device.","","**improvement \u003e 10% (over mean baseline):**","Formula: `(baseline_mae - model_mae) / baseline_mae`. The mean baseline (predict user's mean glucose for everything) is surprisingly hard to beat. A model that only improves 5% isn't worth the complexity — the improvement must be clinically meaningful, not just statistically detectable.","","**p \u003c 0.05 (permutation test, 1000 shuffles):**","Distribution-free significance test. Shuffle glucose labels 1000 times, refit model each time, count how often shuffled r \u003e= observed r. No Gaussian assumption. This catches cases where a high r is an artifact of small sample size or temporal autocorrelation.","","**Result:** 0/22 population stages pass. GP personal models pass for 1/2 live users (a0456651 with 250+ samples).","","---","","## 3. Gaussian Process: Physics-Informed Kernel","","### Why GP Over Ridge/SVR","","Ridge regression assumes linear voice-glucose relationships. After 22 stages showing linear models can't capture the signal, Stage 19 tested GP with nonlinear kernels. Result: GP beats Ridge for 7/10 subjects. The key insight: the voice-glucose relationship is nonlinear and subject-specific — exactly what GP kernels capture.","","### Kernel Architecture (`physics_gp.py`)","","```","K = C(1.0) * RBF(length_scale=[per-feature]) + WhiteKernel(noise=0.5)","```","","**Physics-informed length scales:**","- PITCH features (pitch_mean, pitch_std, f0_cv, jitter_local): length_scale=1.5 (shorter = more sensitive). Motivated by Kaufman 2024 finding that F0 increases 0.02 Hz per mg/dL.","- VOICE features (mfcc_0, mfcc_1, spectral_centroid, shimmer_approx, hnr, voiced_ratio): length_scale=2.5 (longer = less certain about relevance). These features have weaker theoretical links to glucose.","","### Blending Schedule","","- n\u003c10: Ridge only (GP needs minimum data for stable kernel estimation)","- n=10-20: Linear blend from 5% GP to 100% GP","- n\u003e20: GP fully takes over","","**Why n=10 minimum:** GP has O(n^3) complexity and requires sufficient data to estimate kernel hyperparameters. Below 10 samples, the kernel optimization is underdetermined and produces unreliable uncertainty estimates.","","### Production Evidence","","- a0456651 (243 cal): GP MAE 7.15, r=0.779 — passes signal gate","- Same user, Ridge: MAE 13.05, r=0.09 — fails signal gate","- The signal is GP-specific: the nonlinear kernel captures patterns Ridge cannot.","","---","","## 4. Feature Selection","","### personal_10: Why These 10 From 103","","Indices into 103-dim canonical: `[0, 1, 80, 99, 90, 91, 97, 98, 100, 101]`","","| Feature | Why Included |","|---------|-------------|","| mfcc_0_mean | Spectral envelope shape — primary voice timbre descriptor |","| mfcc_1_mean | Spectral slope — voice brightness, complements mfcc_0 |","| spectral_centroid | Frequency center of mass — gain-independent spectral measure |","| shimmer_approx | Amplitude perturbation — gain-independent (normalized), replaces energy_mean |","| pitch_mean | Fundamental frequency — Kaufman 2024: F0 increases 0.02 Hz/mg/dL |","| pitch_std | Pitch variability — may reflect cognitive/autonomic glucose effects |","| f0_cv | Coefficient of variation of F0 — normalized pitch instability |","| jitter_local | Period perturbation — voice quality marker |","| hnr | Harmonics-to-noise ratio — vocal clarity, affected by hydration/fatigue |","| voiced_ratio | Fraction of voiced frames — speech fluency, pausing behavior |","","### Why energy_mean Was Removed (Stage 22)","","energy_mean (index 86) is hardware-dependent — it scales with microphone gain, volume settings, and device distance. A user switching from iPhone to laptop would shift energy_mean dramatically, contaminating the personal model. shimmer_approx (index 99) measures the same amplitude domain but is normalized (ratio of consecutive periods), making it gain-independent.","","### Why Not All 103 Features?","","843 samples / 103 features = 8.2:1 ratio. This is borderline safe for regularized models but fragile. Stages 13-21b tested 2,500+ feature combinations (HuBERT 2304-dim, nonlinear 68-dim, contrastive embeddings, SEED 141-dim). All produced 0 signal improvement on the population level. The bottleneck is data density per user, not feature expressiveness.","","### Why edge_10 Is Legacy","","The original edge_10 set was chosen for on-device computation speed, not signal quality. It included energy_mean (hardware-dependent), formant_f1_mean (unreliable from short clips), and f0_slope (noisy estimate). personal_10 was selected in Stage 22 by analyzing which canonical features best align with GP kernel physics priors and are gain-independent.","","---","","## 5. Data Pipeline Decisions","","### Why ±15 Minute Matching Window","","The DATA_PIPELINE_AUDIT (22 issues) found the original production pipeline used a 60-minute matching window. At 60 minutes, glucose can change 60-180 mg/dL — pairing a voice sample with a glucose reading from an hour later is scientifically invalid.","","Literature standard: Lehmann 2026 (Diabetes Care) and Kaufman 2024 (Sci Rep) use ≤15 minutes. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH recommends \"within 5 min\" for future collection.","","±15 minutes is a practical compromise: strict enough to be scientifically valid, loose enough to retain adequate samples from historical data with imprecise timestamps. Result: 843 matched samples from `rematch_strict_v2.py`.","","### Why No Voice Activity Detection (VAD)","","Tested empirically:","- Without VAD: MAE 10.24, r=0.368","- With VAD: MAE 10.47, r=0.343","","VAD *hurts*. Pauses contain glucose-related information — speech hesitancy, cognitive processing speed, and autonomic effects on breathing patterns are all potential signals that VAD discards. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH explicitly notes: \"Pauses contain glucose-related information.\"","","### Why No Data Augmentation","","The v5 pipeline tested time-stretching and pitch-shifting augmentation. Performance degraded. Rationale: the glucose signal (if it exists) resides in natural vocal characteristics — F0 perturbation, jitter, shimmer, spectral shape. Artificially distorting these destroys exactly the features we're trying to learn from.","","---","","## 6. Adaptive Ensemble","","### tau = 8 (Exponential Blending)","","Formula: `w = 1 - exp(-n / tau)`, where w is personal model weight and n is calibration count.","","| n | w (personal weight) |","|---|-------------------|","| 5 | 0.47 (47%) |","| 8 | 0.63 (63%) |","| 10 | 0.71 (71%) |","| 20 | 0.92 (92%) |","","Originally tau=30 (conservative). Lowered to 8 in Stage 22 because:","1. Population model has no signal (r=-0.098) — relying on it longer provides zero benefit","2. Personal model should dominate sooner","3. Temporal prior fills the gap before personal model activates","4. Synced everywhere: SDK, server, dashboard","","### Ridge Alpha = 100/n (Inverse Sample Regularization)","","| n | alpha | Effect |","|---|-------|--------|","| 5 | 20.0 | Heavy regularization — prevents overfitting on 5 samples |","| 20 | 5.0 | Moderate |","| 100 | 1.0 | Light — enough data to support model complexity |","","Inverse scaling balances model complexity with sample size. Small personal datasets (n\u003c30) are particularly prone to overfitting with 10 features. VOICE_GLUCOSE_FROM_SCRATCH notes this is \"an arbitrary heuristic, never formally validated\" — it was tuned from original 10/n to 100/n based on empirical testing with live users.","","---","","## 7. Hypo Detection","","### Threshold: \u003c80 mg/dL (Not Clinical \u003c70)","","Clinical hypoglycemia is defined as \u003c70 mg/dL, but our dataset has only 7 samples below 70 versus 45 below 80. Training a classifier on 7 positive samples is unreliable. The 80 mg/dL threshold is a pragmatic choice to have sufficient training data while still detecting clinically relevant low glucose events. Future: lower to \u003c70 once 20+ sub-70 samples are available per user.","","### Three-Layer Architecture","","1. **RuleBasedHypoDetector**: 5 biomarker rules (high pitch variability, high jitter, low F0, low energy, low voiced ratio). Alert when \u003e=2 fire. No training needed — works from calibration 1.","2. **ClassifierHypoDetector**: LogisticRegression + SMOTE (handles class imbalance). Gated by AUROC \u003e 0.65 with \u003e=80% sensitivity threshold. Only activates when gate passes.","3. **HybridHypoDetector**: If classifier is active and passes gate, use classifier OR rules. If classifier fails gate, fall back to rules only.","","### Why SMOTE","","Hypo events are rare (45/843 = 5.3%). Without oversampling, LogReg ignores the minority class. SMOTE synthesizes artificial hypo samples in feature space. The AUROC \u003e 0.65 gate ensures we don't deploy a classifier that's just guessing.","","**Results:** Population AUROC 0.516 (fails gate). Personal: 4/6 subjects pass (Margarita 0.781, Sybille 0.938, Wolf 0.794, Darav 0.760).","","---","","## 8. Background Training Architecture","","### 6-Hour Cycle (BackgroundTrainer)","","- Frequent enough to catch signal emergence within a day of active calibration","- Infrequent enough to respect Render API limits and avoid blocking the event loop","- Real-world: most users don't calibrate faster than every 2-4 hours","","### 24-Hour Cycle (ExperimentSweep)","","Broader config search (60+ configs vs BackgroundTrainer's 14). Runs daily because:","- Wider search is computationally expensive","- Config landscape changes slowly (new calibrations trickle in)","- Gate: requires 3+ users with 5+ calibrations each (population-level experiments)","","### Sample Gates by Task","","| Task | Minimum Samples | Rationale |","|------|----------------|-----------|","| Personal Ridge | 5 | Minimum for 10-feature regression |","| Config search | 5 | Multi-config exploration |","| GP model | 10 | O(n^3) stability, kernel estimation |","| Hypo detection | 10 | Need ~2+ hypo events minimum |","| Signal detection | 20 | Temporal CV needs enough for train+test |","| Population models | 5 users × 5 cals | Cross-user generalization |","","### asyncio.to_thread() Pattern","","Critical bug (Mar 17): synchronous sklearn model fitting blocked the asyncio event loop. Render's health check (`/health`) never responded during training → API marked DOWN. Fix: wrap all `_evaluate_*` calls in `asyncio.to_thread()` + 60s startup delay (trainer) + 120s (sweep). **Rule: never run sklearn/GP sync code directly in async handlers.**","","---","","## 9. Feature Space Alignment (SDK v2.6.0)","","### The Two Critical Bugs","","**Bug 1: Log Scale Mismatch (Fixed v2.5.0)**","- JS SDK: `Math.log(power)` (natural log)","- Python/librosa: `10 * Math.log10(power)` (decibels)","- Factor: 4.3429x — features were in completely different scales","","**Bug 2: Mel Filterbank Mismatch (Fixed v2.6.0)**","- JS SDK: HTK formula `2595 * log10(1 + hz/700)`, no bandwidth normalization","- Python/librosa: Slaney (piecewise linear/log) + `norm='slaney'`","- Result: MFCC correlation **-0.82** between SDK and server (anti-correlated!)","","### Migration Strategy","","- 327 Supabase calibrations migrated (log fix + `_mel_scale='htk'` flag on old data)","- On-device samples flagged `_mel_scale='htk'` in localStorage","- Models train on both HTK and Slaney features; tau=8 weighting naturally phases out old samples","- Cannot retroactively convert HTK→Slaney without re-extracting from raw audio (which was already deleted per privacy policy)","","### Lesson","","When porting DSP algorithms to JS, verify EVERY parameter (log base, mel formula, normalization flags) against the reference implementation. Comments saying \"matches librosa\" don't guarantee it. Always validate with correlation tests on the same audio files.","","---","","## 10. Conformal Prediction","","### Coverage Target: 80-90% (Not 95%)","","95% prediction intervals are too wide for clinical utility — \"your glucose is between 60 and 180\" is useless. 80% intervals are tighter and more actionable. The trade-off: 20% of true values fall outside the interval, but the interval itself is narrow enough to guide decisions.","","**Implementation:** Quantile regression learns upper/lower bounds from data. No Gaussian assumption (voice features and glucose are both skewed). Stage 19 results: 80.9% average coverage (target 90%), average width 52.9 mg/dL.","","---","","## 11. Population vs Personal: The Core Finding","","### 22 Stages of Honest Negatives","","Every population-level approach failed the signal gate:","- Stages 1-12: Pipeline setup, Edge Impulse debunked (data leakage), infrastructure","- Stage 13: HuBERT, Glottal, MAML — 0/9 signal","- Stage 14: Nonlinear features (entropy, fractal, TEO, wavelet) — 0/63 signal","- Stage 15: Contrastive learning (CNN embeddings) — 0/11 signal","- Stage 16: Quintile classification, asymmetric matching — 0/27 signal","- Stage 17: Dual-track contextual model — useful temporal prior, no voice signal","- Stage 18: Hypo detection — personal works, population fails","- Stage 19: GP — beats Ridge personally, still no population signal","- Stage 20: SEED dynamics — 0/16 signal","- Stage 21: Windowed models — 3/10 improved personally","- Stage 21b: Delta features — hurt 10/10; CGM rate_of_change is label leakage","","### What Actually Works","","1. **Personal GP models** (Stage 19): GP beats Ridge 7/10 subjects. Nonlinear kernel captures individual voice-glucose patterns that linear models miss.","2. **Temporal prior** (Stage 17): Smart clock — \"what's your glucose usually at this time of day?\" Works from calibration 1.","3. **Personal hypo detection** (Stage 18): 4/6 subjects pass AUROC gate. Useful safety net.","4. **Excursion detection** (Stage 19): GP uncertainty flags abnormal predictions. Sensitivity 0.50, specificity 0.97.","","### Product Implication","","The product is personal adaptation + temporal prior + hypo detection, NOT population voice-glucose prediction. Recruiting CGM users for paired data is the path forward — personal models need data density (200+ samples per user), not breadth (more subjects with 50 samples each).","","---","","## 12. Device Change Detection (Stage 22)","","### Problem","","Users switch phones, browsers, or recording environments. Each device has different microphone characteristics (gain, frequency response, noise floor). A personal model trained on iPhone Safari data will perform poorly on Chrome Desktop data — the feature distributions shift.","","### Solution (`_filter_device_change()`)","","Group calibrations by device fingerprint: `{os}_{browser}_{platform}`. When the newest device has 15+ samples, drop all samples from older devices. This prevents cross-device feature contamination while ensuring the model always has enough data from the current device.","","### Why 15 Samples","","Below 15, dropping old data might leave too few samples for reliable Ridge/GP fitting. Above 15, the new device has enough data to stand alone. This threshold was chosen to balance device purity against sample scarcity.","","---","","## 13. Quality Metadata (Stage 22)","","### Soft Gate (Not Hard Gate)","","The SDK's `addCalibration()` checks four quality criteria:","- Duration \u003c 2s (too short for reliable features)","- Voiced ratio \u003c 0.25 (mostly silence/noise)","- Energy \u003e 0.5 (clipping)","- Energy \u003c 0.001 (near-silence)","","Failures produce warnings but **still store the calibration**. Rationale: rejecting data loses information that might be valuable. Instead, quality scores are passed as sample weights to the GP model — low-quality samples have higher noise variance, reducing their influence without discarding them entirely.","","---","","## 14. Supabase JSON Column Patterns","","### dict Before list (Critical)","","Supabase returns JSON columns as Python dicts: `{\"0\": 1.23, \"1\": 4.56, ...}` not lists `[1.23, 4.56, ...]`. This caused 3 critical silent-failure bugs where `isinstance(fv, list)` skipped every calibration.","","**Rule:** Always check `isinstance(x, dict)` BEFORE `isinstance(x, list)` when parsing feature_vector, model_artifact, or any Supabase JSON column.","","### Metadata Keys in Feature Dicts","","Feature vector dicts may contain non-numeric keys: `_mel_scale`, `_migrated_to_db`, etc. Never use `range(len(fv))` to iterate — use `range(N_FEATURES)` or `sum(1 for k in fv if k.isdigit())` to count actual features. This caused data drops in 12 locations (fixed Mar 19).","","---","","## 15. Competitive Analysis Context","","| Study | Claim | Reality |","|-------|-------|---------|","| Lehmann 2026 (Diabetes Care) | AUC 0.90 for hypo | Detects emergency state, not continuous glucose |","| Guo 2025 (J Voice) | 95.2% AUC | Includes HbA1c + fasting glucose as inputs; voice-only = 80.8% |","| Kaufman 2024 (Sci Rep) | F0 correlates with glucose | F0 increases 0.02 Hz/mg/dL — real but tiny (3.3 Hz over full range) |","","None attempt continuous glucose regression from naturalistic voice. ONVOX's honest negative results (0/22 population stages) and positive personal results (GP MAE 7.15 for top user) are novel contributions to the field."],"stylingDirectives":[[[0,27,"pl-mh"],[2,27,"pl-en"]],[[0,1,"pl-s"],[62,63,"pl-s"]],[],[],[],[[0,3,"pl-ms"]],[],[[0,28,"pl-mh"],[3,28,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,46,"pl-mh"],[4,46,"pl-en"]],[],[[39,40,"pl-s"],[46,47,"pl-s"],[68,69,"pl-s"],[73,74,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[18,19,"pl-s"],[19,33,"pl-c1"],[33,34,"pl-s"],[36,38,"pl-s"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"],[2,3,"pl-s"],[3,24,"pl-c1"],[24,25,"pl-s"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"],[2,3,"pl-s"],[3,32,"pl-c1"],[32,33,"pl-s"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[],[[0,47,"pl-mh"],[4,47,"pl-en"]],[],[[63,64,"pl-s"],[82,83,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,55,"pl-mh"],[4,55,"pl-en"]],[],[[19,20,"pl-s"],[20,46,"pl-c1"],[46,47,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,3,"pl-ms"]],[],[[0,27,"pl-mh"],[3,27,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,62,"pl-mh"],[4,62,"pl-en"]],[],[],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[34,36,"pl-s"]],[],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[41,43,"pl-s"]],[[9,10,"pl-s"],[10,51,"pl-c1"],[51,52,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[45,47,"pl-s"]],[],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[9,11,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,3,"pl-ms"]],[],[[0,47,"pl-mh"],[3,47,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,25,"pl-mh"],[4,25,"pl-en"]],[],[],[],[[0,41,"pl-mh"],[4,41,"pl-en"],[25,26,"pl-s"],[26,39,"pl-c1"],[39,40,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,3,"pl-s"],[3,3,"pl-c1"]],[[0,69,"pl-c1"]],[[0,0,"pl-c1"],[0,3,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[33,35,"pl-s"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[],[[0,21,"pl-mh"],[4,21,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[],[[0,2,"pl-s"],[19,21,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,23,"pl-mh"],[4,23,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[[0,1,"pl-v"]],[],[[0,3,"pl-ms"]],[],[[0,23,"pl-mh"],[3,23,"pl-en"]],[],[[0,38,"pl-mh"],[4,38,"pl-en"]],[],[[32,33,"pl-s"],[33,73,"pl-c1"],[73,74,"pl-s"]],[],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[10,11,"pl-ml"],[25,26,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[10,11,"pl-ml"],[24,25,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[14,15,"pl-ml"],[74,75,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[14,15,"pl-ml"],[70,71,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[20,21,"pl-ml"],[83,84,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[17,18,"pl-ml"],[96,97,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[13,14,"pl-ml"],[80,81,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[12,13,"pl-ml"],[82,83,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"],[8,9,"pl-ml"],[72,73,"pl-ml"]],[[0,1,"pl-ml"] aria-labelledby="file-name-id-wide file-name-id-mobile" class="BlobContent-module__blobContentSection__VOgZq BlobContent-module__blobContentSectionMarkdown__mPLOK" style="margin-top:46px"><div class="Box-sc-62in7e-0 js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned BlobContent-module__markdownBlob__T8jpG" data-hpc="true"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">ONVOX Technical Rationale</h1><a id="user-content-onvox-technical-rationale" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: ONVOX Technical Rationale" href="#onvox-technical-rationale"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>Written: Mar 22, 2026 — Covers all decisions through Stage 22</em></p>
<p dir="auto">This document explains WHY every major technical decision was made, grounded in empirical evidence, research literature, and lessons from 22 research stages on 843 samples across 11 subjects.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">1. Validation Methodology</h2><a id="user-content-1-validation-methodology" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 1. Validation Methodology" href="#1-validation-methodology"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Why Chronological Splits (Not Shuffled CV)</h3><a id="user-content-why-chronological-splits-not-shuffled-cv" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Why Chronological Splits (Not Shuffled CV)" href="#why-chronological-splits-not-shuffled-cv"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Standard k-fold CV and LOO-CV train on <em>future</em> data to predict the <em>past</em>. In production, only past data exists. Shuffled CV consistently overestimates performance — Stage 15 showed contrastive learning achieved MAE 4.81 with "unified" (shuffled) evaluation but 14.85+ with honest LOSO. This 3x gap is pure data leakage.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Implementation (<code>temporal_cv.py</code>):</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>chronological_split()</code>: Sort by timestamp, train on first 70%, test on last 30%</li>
<li><code>expanding_window_validation()</code>: Train on samples 1..K, predict K+1, then 1..K+1 predict K+2, etc.</li>
<li>Threshold: expanding-window if n&gt;=50 (enough windows), otherwise 70/30</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Why LOSO Is the Honest Population Benchmark</h3><a id="user-content-why-loso-is-the-honest-population-benchmark" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Why LOSO Is the Honest Population Benchmark" href="#why-loso-is-the-honest-population-benchmark"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Leave-One-Subject-Out cross-validation tests generalization to <em>unseen individuals</em>. This is the only valid test for a population model because production users are never in the training set. All 22 stages report LOSO as the primary metric. Result: best population LOSO is SVR MAE 12.48, r=-0.098 — effectively no signal.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Why Held-Out Validation (80/20 Chronological Blind)</h3><a id="user-content-why-held-out-validation-8020-chronological-blind" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Why Held-Out Validation (80/20 Chronological Blind)" href="#why-held-out-validation-8020-chronological-blind"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Added in Stage 22 (<code>tools/validate_held_out.py</code>) as the strictest personal model test. Train on first 80% of a user's data, predict last 20% — data the model has never seen, in chronological order. Result: a0456651 GP MAE 7.92, r=0.604, p=0.001 — first model to pass the signal gate on properly held-out data.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2. Signal Detection Gate</h2><a id="user-content-2-signal-detection-gate" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2. Signal Detection Gate" href="#2-signal-detection-gate"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Three-Part AND Logic: r&gt;0.3 AND improvement&gt;10% AND p&lt;0.05</h3><a id="user-content-three-part-and-logic-r03-and-improvement10-and-p005" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Three-Part AND Logic: r&gt;0.3 AND improvement&gt;10% AND p&lt;0.05" href="#three-part-and-logic-r03-and-improvement10-and-p005"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">All three must pass simultaneously. This prevents false discovery across 22 stages of testing.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>r &gt; 0.3 (correlation threshold):</strong>
Detects meaningful linear association without requiring strong signal. Below 0.3, the correlation explains &lt;9% of variance — indistinguishable from noise on small samples. This is conservative: clinical biomarkers typically require r&gt;0.5, but we're searching for signal, not certifying a device.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>improvement &gt; 10% (over mean baseline):</strong>
Formula: <code>(baseline_mae - model_mae) / baseline_mae</code>. The mean baseline (predict user's mean glucose for everything) is surprisingly hard to beat. A model that only improves 5% isn't worth the complexity — the improvement must be clinically meaningful, not just statistically detectable.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>p &lt; 0.05 (permutation test, 1000 shuffles):</strong>
Distribution-free significance test. Shuffle glucose labels 1000 times, refit model each time, count how often shuffled r &gt;= observed r. No Gaussian assumption. This catches cases where a high r is an artifact of small sample size or temporal autocorrelation.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Result:</strong> 0/22 population stages pass. GP personal models pass for 1/2 live users (a0456651 with 250+ samples).</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3. Gaussian Process: Physics-Informed Kernel</h2><a id="user-content-3-gaussian-process-physics-informed-kernel" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3. Gaussian Process: Physics-Informed Kernel" href="#3-gaussian-process-physics-informed-kernel"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Why GP Over Ridge/SVR</h3><a id="user-content-why-gp-over-ridgesvr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Why GP Over Ridge/SVR" href="#why-gp-over-ridgesvr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Ridge regression assumes linear voice-glucose relationships. After 22 stages showing linear models can't capture the signal, Stage 19 tested GP with nonlinear kernels. Result: GP beats Ridge for 7/10 subjects. The key insight: the voice-glucose relationship is nonlinear and subject-specific — exactly what GP kernels capture.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Kernel Architecture (<code>physics_gp.py</code>)</h3><a id="user-content-kernel-architecture-physics_gppy" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Kernel Architecture (physics_gp.py)" href="#kernel-architecture-physics_gppy"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="K = C(1.0) * RBF(length_scale=[per-feature]) + WhiteKernel(noise=0.5)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>K = C(1.0) * RBF(length_scale=[per-feature]) + WhiteKernel(noise=0.5)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Physics-informed length scales:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>PITCH features (pitch_mean, pitch_std, f0_cv, jitter_local): length_scale=1.5 (shorter = more sensitive). Motivated by Kaufman 2024 finding that F0 increases 0.02 Hz per mg/dL.</li>
<li>VOICE features (mfcc_0, mfcc_1, spectral_centroid, shimmer_approx, hnr, voiced_ratio): length_scale=2.5 (longer = less certain about relevance). These features have weaker theoretical links to glucose.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Blending Schedule</h3><a id="user-content-blending-schedule" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Blending Schedule" href="#blending-schedule"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>n&lt;10: Ridge only (GP needs minimum data for stable kernel estimation)</li>
<li>n=10-20: Linear blend from 5% GP to 100% GP</li>
<li>n&gt;20: GP fully takes over</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Why n=10 minimum:</strong> GP has O(n^3) complexity and requires sufficient data to estimate kernel hyperparameters. Below 10 samples, the kernel optimization is underdetermined and produces unreliable uncertainty estimates.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Production Evidence</h3><a id="user-content-production-evidence" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Production Evidence" href="#production-evidence"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>a0456651 (243 cal): GP MAE 7.15, r=0.779 — passes signal gate</li>
<li>Same user, Ridge: MAE 13.05, r=0.09 — fails signal gate</li>
<li>The signal is GP-specific: the nonlinear kernel captures patterns Ridge cannot.</li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">4. Feature Selection</h2><a id="user-content-4-feature-selection" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 4. Feature Selection" href="#4-feature-selection"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">personal_10: Why These 10 From 103</h3><a id="user-content-personal_10-why-these-10-from-103" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: personal_10: Why These 10 From 103" href="#personal_10-why-these-10-from-103"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Indices into 103-dim canonical: <code>[0, 1, 80, 99, 90, 91, 97, 98, 100, 101]</code></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Feature</th>
<th>Why Included</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>mfcc_0_mean</td>
<td>Spectral envelope shape — primary voice timbre descriptor</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>mfcc_1_mean</td>
<td>Spectral slope — voice brightness, complements mfcc_0</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>spectral_centroid</td>
<td>Frequency center of mass — gain-independent spectral measure</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>shimmer_approx</td>
<td>Amplitude perturbation — gain-independent (normalized), replaces energy_mean</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>pitch_mean</td>
<td>Fundamental frequency — Kaufman 2024: F0 increases 0.02 Hz/mg/dL</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>pitch_std</td>
<td>Pitch variability — may reflect cognitive/autonomic glucose effects</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>f0_cv</td>
<td>Coefficient of variation of F0 — normalized pitch instability</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>jitter_local</td>
<td>Period perturbation — voice quality marker</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>hnr</td>
<td>Harmonics-to-noise ratio — vocal clarity, affected by hydration/fatigue</td>
</tr>
